We must find ways to involve the most backward masses in the club, without sacrificing
keeping in mind the main tasks of the club. This can be achieved by pouring
joint efforts of a number of cultural institutions.

Therefore, any attempt to monopolize club work and
to be its only leader, not only organizational, but
and ideological - this attempt, which is now being undertaken by the profeo-
zami, can lead to the same degeneration and internal disintegration
the wave of clubs that took place in previous years. Over time
I will no longer need some of the details specified here, but in the absence
any club practice, except that which is carried out monopoly
ny organization, the slightest incorrect deviation in its work can
lead to disaster.

Moscow, 1923

Dear comrades!
Today, on the anniversary of the execution of the Lena workers, I am at the water lift;

Saratov station made a report about Lenskoh execution. Served as material for me

book by T. V. F. Pletnev, published by the All-Russian Proletkult in 1923.
Despite the fact that it was absolutely impossible to cover everything in an hour and a half
material contained in the book, however, this book gave a lot
paintings and performances for me and my comrades from the water-lifting station. I
I don’t remember a single report of mine at this same water pumping station, so that t.t. workers
listened with such interest and attention. I now imagine one hundred
Rick the toolmaker, who, with all my reports that I gave, usually

07
214 Ohm. No. 8

he always sat with his head down and his eyes closed, so that it was difficult to determine—
does he listen or fall asleep; this comrade was sitting at the same report, and his eyes
glittered, he looked at me point-blank and shook his head to the beat. Particularly attentive
Actually, my comrades listened to excerpts from the book when I read them some passages,
e.g.: “Legal and everyday situation of workers” (testimonies of workers’ wives about the “right
first night”), Comrade worker’s story about the execution on April 4 (“The situation at the prison
claims from the beginning of the strike until April 4th“).

Despite the fact that my comrades were very tired, they were ready to listen
as much as you like.

It seems to me that this book is very good - not only as a historical
description, but also for workers to read. I really regret only one thing in it
there are no good photographic photographs of the area where the execution took place, and of the
type of Lena mines. And, if you can express it as a wish, then good
It would be nice to include these photos. The testimony of the photographer Ko-va states that
he took a picture of the execution, but the police officer took the camera and the negative from him. Not me-
It would be crazy to look in the archives of the secret police and find this negative. Photographs
will help comrade workers imagine the harsh climate of Siberia, and all those rivers, oh
which are mentioned at the beginning of the book and which are an empty phrase for the workers.

Personally, I would also like to point out that at the beginning of the book there are a lot of numbers.
In Tables 1 and 3 you can give the numbers of the results, and tlooks like a scientific work
or to an official report. The worker will skip these columns of numbers. They are needed
condense and explain more. Still, you definitely need to insert into the book:
what role did party workers play in this strike? In general—
the book is good. s

From comrade Hello N. Remizov.

Comrade's answer. Remizov. Dear comrade!

I consider it my duty to respond to your review of my book about the Lena events.
tiyah. Judging by your review, the book gave you material for an interesting report
about the Lena events. That's the way it should be. The Lena events cannot be
interesting for our comrades. Speaker, well Bolar and having worked -
Any material about the Lena events will always be interesting. I completely agree with you
that the book contains a number of shortcomings. Haste to work with lack of time
me (the entire book was written in my free time, which I had
very little), of course, affected her.

But I would like to answer you on the further lines of your letter.

You are not satisfied that the book begins with numbers. This is the same remark
Other comrades also lamented to me, but I stubbornly adhere to the opinion that the beginning of the book
there's nothing wrong with the numbers, and here's why.

Those 3800-4000 poods of gold that were mined in Russia were worth the position of the
barrels on Lena. After all, in other places the situation of gold miners
it was no better, except that there were no salvos on April 4th. This production is estimated
amounted to 7 (approximately) billion rubles in gold, i.e., a two-year budget
Russia during tsarism. 7.

I wanted these numbers to attract the reader's attention. To
bare figures of the era of tsarism, calm, cold witnesses of the cruel
exploitation, he learned to see life. We are not used to reading numbers, first of all
vykh, and clothe them with flesh and blood, secondly. And you need to learn this. First
part of the book is structured in such a way that 1!/5-2 pages with numbers do not tire, but further
This presentation becomes livelier, and you will still remember that gold is mined in Russia
moose is about 4,000 poods per year. And this is alreadyresult. There is also further
lifrs, and they are not criticized, because the interest of events is already pushing towards them.
%#°

No. 8 BIBLIOGRAPHY, 215

This is the first thing. Second: the book costs just 2 thousand, due to the haste of release,
came out without photos; in the remaining 7 thousand - with photographs. Therefore,
This deficiency has been eliminated. And one more note. The book contains a play like
an artistic summary of events, and I would very much like that fellow speakers
in the history of the Lena events it has always been emphasized that the history of the labor movement
provides inexhaustible material for artistic creativity. I think this is over-
extremely important. Our struggle for a good fifty years has yielded powerful
pictures, which are the task of the proletariat to understand. And in celebration of this, I turn and
to you and to all comrades with a request to remember this slogan thrown by the Pro-
Letkult back in 1920: “The history of the labor movement must become material
for the artistic creativity of the proletariat." Otherwise I did everything I could.
If the book requires a 2nd edition, of course it will be corrected and will be more complete.

activities and methods of self-education and researcheating work.

cabinet" (No. 2), an interesting and important question about the method of
dah scientific and creative work. The need for urgent preparation of young workers
scientists—Marxists—causes an attempt to systematize the existing scientific
material and organization of creative work on the principle of collective, factory-
no work. The fight against the chaotic growth of literature, against parallelism in research
dedicated work, with subjectivity of assessment for systematic, standardized
production of scientific goods

“Science, in its general methods of organization, has lagged far behind production.
of material goods,” notes Comrade Aptekar,

“Two conditions for victory on the ideological front”—put forward by Comrade Mayorsky
(No. 3, “Conditions of Victory”); first: everyday communication between young communists and older
ry party members, joint work, joint club life, etc.; second;
factory method of scientific labor with division of labor functions-{ „electrification-
cation of scientific work“, i.e. industrial organization of science.

This question in terms of mastering knowledge is of enormous importance for us.
of today's communist youth. It wouldn’t hurt for our “people” to think about it.

The evolution of the left front, from the first experience of futurism with revolutionary
street to the proclamation of the production principle in art - trace-
is stated by one of the theorists of the magazine, N. Chuzhak, in his articles “Under the sign
life-building” (program) and “Tasks of the day” (discussion).

Futurism, as a school, it turns out, is denied by Lef, and is only recognized
futurism as an aspiration.

“Art,” Lef believes, “since it is still thought of by us as time-
variable, until complete dissolution in life, unique, built on
the use of emotions, activity is the production of what the class and people need
honor of values (things).”

The theorists of futurism in 1918 denied the so-called “idea of things”—
“Lef” is now introducing an amendment:

“Since ideological values built on dialectical awareness
world, are accepted by us (like material ones) only from the angle of their purpose.
nia, - to that extent there can be no talk of negating the “idea of things.” .

Not only a tangible thing, but also an idea, a thing in a model - is the content of use.
art of the day.

Hence the acceptance of all kinds of experimentalth art, from bio-mech-
preparatory steps before building peace through dialectical mono-
delimitation (constructivism, symbolism).

All kinds of fantasy, utopianism and other holo-ideological, metaphysical
quirks that are not based on the dialectical refraction of reality, fabricated
are busy.

So the “distortions of reality” that repelled the theorists of 1918—
from now on are recognized as still necessary stages of creativity, but in the presence of only
identifying and confronting contradictions.

Under the sign of effective life-building comes the science of the proletariat about the use of
art. Under the sign of overcoming, as opposed to the expelled weak-willedness of perception,
tia—his attitude to the process of art-building is built. Under the sign of the strong-willed
sharpening of the apparatus, in the striving for communism—we imagine the art of the day.

Yesenin. Yesenin has already firmly entered Russian literature. He
FAVORITES becomes a classic. Publication of his poems by Gosizdat as
> By myself. would officially assign this position to him. But then
Moscow. 1929, what is collected in this collection was hardly “chosen” by ourselves
< ; Yesenin, because many of the best things were not included in it
poet, such as “Sorokoust”, “Confession of a Hooligan”, etc., must be because
that some expressions in them seemed pictorial to the guardians of “morality”
bathrooms in the poetic lexicon,

The book was compiled according tomainly from early works taken from
collections “Radunitsa”, “Dove”, “Treryadnitsa”, in which Yesenin acted as
"peasant" poet. Therefore, the characterization of Yesenin from the book “Favorites” is not
may be exhaustive. So, for example, at least the metrical construction of verses,
according to a rough estimate, it is expressed in the following figures: out of 52 verses, co-
compiling the collection, 50%/) are written in trochee, 270// in iambic, 17/ in free verse,
6'/›--dactylem. Meanwhile, in relation to everything written by Yesenin,
the number of free verses outside the meter should be significantly increased, because more
later pieces not included in the collection were written primarily in free style.
home The same must be said about rhyme. In this collection, rhyme gram-
tic, whereas in later things it is more often consonant.

Complex technical and compositional tasks posed by Russian poetry
over the past two decades, are alien to Yesenin.

Compositionally, Yesenin's verse is constructed in the most simplified way. This—
a series of four-line stanzas united by rhymes of the first line with the third, second

Siberian.

I)
224 t FR s: No. 8

swarm—from the fourth. In order to achieve compositional unity, he often joins
runs in the construction of stanzas to the “ring”, also very primitive, although widespread
strange reception. Complex forms of rondo and sonnet are not found in his works at all.
He has no original rhythmic variations that break the monotony of the meter.
a lot. The sound texture of the word is also not characteristic of his verse.

The main core of Yesenin's poetry is the image. Imagists claim
that where there is no image, there is no poetry. Every thought, feeling, idea is only
then they are worthy of being called poetic when they are clothed in the flesh of artistic
new image. The image is the body and soul of poetry. Yesenin’s image has a number of special
richness. The pictorial side of his images is the rural landscape.
The metaphor of an image is usually built along a descending line: a more general phenomenon
order and greater significance, he endows the properties of phenomena for more than an hourtnyh
and lesser significance. Previous poets usually personified an everyday object
into some “sublime” image. Yesenin does the opposite. He's the sun
compares it to a wheel, the moon to a frog. A distinctive feature of his images is
their anthropomorphism. He endows nature with the properties of humans or animals.
Autumn for him is a “red mare”, the wind is a schema-monk who “crumples the foliage along the way”
road stupas,” the month is a lamb, the hut is an old woman, the sunset is a red swan, blue
dusk—a flock of sheep. “No one would even think that straw is also flesh,”
he says, but he “gets up” so constantly that the road can start thinking about “red-
this evening”, that “an old maple on one leg” can guard “blue Rus'”,
that a month can float and drop oars on lakes, etc.

The coloring of Yesenin's poetry is typical of him; reactionistic: evening - green,
grass is blue, dusk is blue, Russia is blue, “ash is green from a pink oven.”
Remember Degas, Monet, Renoir. The most common color is blue. At 52
poems in the collection—blue, as an adjective to define iveta, meeting
occurs 26 times. At one point he even admits that the blue “sucks his eyes.” Zo-
Lotoy occurs 24 times as a color, blue, green and white—
11 times each, red - 10, pink and yellow - 7 each. These are exactly the colors that
loved by the impressionists. The love for gold brings Yesenin closer to the Russian people -
great art from ancient icons to handicraft toys. Black color, banished
completely from the impressionist palette, also not typical of Yesenin. How
coloration, it occurs only twice.

Yesenin’s extreme subjectivity of perception also brings him closer to the impressionists.
and sketchy manner of writing. Most of his things are just sketches. In landscapes
Yesenin is not a person, as a specific character. Inspiring nature. he
as if he dissolves a person in it, endowing it with human means. No
in his lyrics, very intimate, and Eros. Erotica is alien to him even when he is from
“constipation” introduces someone too “risky” into poetryzi image. In this
In the collection, only one poem is dedicated to a woman. All his love is on-
headed to the homeland. Not to Russia, but to Rus'. He is looking for the most tender words
for its definitions: “My land, thoughtful and gentle,” “Oh, Rus', raspberry field,”
“Golden Rus'”, “Oh, you” My Rus', dear Motherland”, “Meek Motherland”. And just like
this was encountered more than once in previous Russian poetry, this motif is intertwined with that
Sky. But his melancholy. in Russia - “merry melancholy.” “And Rus' slumbers in its melancholy,
loy". His sadness is joyful sadness; “Blessed is he who marked with joy your shepherding-
"Such sadness." This is not patriotism, because patriotism is a worldview. It's just de-
rhubarb love. Not a thought, but an emotion. “If the holy army shouts, throw
You are Rus', live in paradise, - I will say: there is no need for paradise, give me my homeland.” This ingenuousness
This village love, cheerful in its melancholy and joyful in sadness, is far away, everything
well, from Blok’s broken love for Russia. For the latter, emotion is inseparable: from
reflections, delight - from pain, love - from patriotism - from

It would be in vain to look for a philosophical worldview in Yesenin’s poetry,
especially expressions of the class ideology of the peasantry. He is essentially not cre-
No. 8 BIBLIOGRAPHY. 225

styansky, but a village poet. He is a village landscape painter, intimately in love
into nature, like the Barbizon painters. In Yesenin’s poetry not only is there no
foundations of the worldview, but, on the contrary, it reflected anarchist psychology
declassed semi-intellectual. “If I weren’t a poet, then I probably would have been
a swindler and a thief." And: “I myself am a robber and a boor, and by blood a steppe horse thief.” „To me
“I wish I could stand in the blue steppe at night, somewhere with a flail.” “But I’m also for someone-
I’m cutting under the autumn whistle.”

Our poetry reflected the psychology of the landowner, the intellectual, in the proletarian
poetry - worker. In the person of Yesenin, she reflected the psychology of a “hooligan.” Until now
Since then, this psychology has found expression in ditties, non-book poetry, oral
noah, folk. In the epics of sleep, it was wrapped in heroic images. "Hooliganism"
Yesenin does not containin itself > dark pathological sides. This is not Apacheism. and
not a decadent breakdown. This is village bravado, the cheerful enthusiasm of the village
the guy that Yesenin essentially is. As in the village, as a boy, he
was a “horse handler” in fights and fun, which he tells you about in his autobiography.
fii, and now he wants to “win” in poetry. Despite the threats “for-
cut * - he is a great romantic and “lyricist”.

Yesenin’s poetry is ideologically pseudo-folk, as it was with Kol-
[tsova, Nikitina, Nekrasova. The modernity of sleep coincides with increased nervousness
ity, but ideologically it is far from modernity. Revolutionism is alien
to her essentially. She is passive, not effective. The revolution received responses in her
like distant lightning, like a reflection. There is only one poem in the book “Favorites”
The work is dedicated to revolution. According to their attachments to the old, Tsedovskaya
village, with a plow and a plow, he is just as eclectic and a direct parallel, for example, Bu-
Nina, as a poet of the passing life of a landowner. Yesenin does not call himself new
poet. This is his distance from the futurists and even his conflict with them. He's all

°in old, rustic, wooden, “hut” Rus'. as Klyuev called her in verse,

dedicated to Yesenin. “I am the last poet of the village,” he says to himself, “and when
a new “iron guest” will come to the fields and the tractor will replace the “foolish horse”, then
his songs no longer “live.” In his significant “Sorokoust” he celebrates
commemoration of the old village, receding into the past, as the place faded into history’
shchichi life. .

Having sung a song, as he promised in one poem, about “the oven, the rooster,
cows,” he stood at a crossroads. Modernity is passing him by. "You are the heart
he made a song for the hut, but did not build a house in his heart,” he says, turning these words
to Klyuev. But with no less reason I could attribute them to myself. Charter "to live"
in his native land,” he goes. “to look for a wretched dwelling” and, like other eclectics,
turns back into the past of history (“Pugachev”) and there wants to find those images that
which modernity does not give him.

IGi 1\ SESSION OF THE ALL-RUSSIAN PROLETKULT Central Committee.

The 3rd session of the Plenum of the Central Committee of Proletkult took place on November 17 - 21 last
1922.

24 thousand people came to the session. (including: 12 workers and 12 intellectuals, from
There are 20 of them communists).

In addition to the Presidium of the Central Committee, Proletkults were represented at the Plenum: Mos-
kovsky, Petrogradsky, Ivanovo-Voznesensky, Tverskoy, Tula, Ekaterinburg-
Sky, Izhevsk, Saratov, Rybinsk, Smolensk, Rzhevsk and Org-Bureau
Ukrainian Proletkult. Representatives of
Agitprop of the Central Committee of the Party.

The Plenum heard the following reports: 1) informational, 2) organizational
ny, 3) reports from the field, 4) report of the Presidium of the Central Committee of Proletkult, proposed
in a number of reports on Departments - Scientific, Arts, Literary Publishing, Financial
Household parts and the Secretariat.

Work in progress. ^2988 was divided into sections: organizational, club and
financial and economic, as a result of which the Plenum adopted a number of
resolutions, their main provisions are as follows.

1. Resolution on an organizational issue.

1. Plenum, stating that since the 2nd Congress of Proletkult there has been no
there were no changes in the sense of the position of Proletkult in the general system of state
authorities neither legally nor in fact, nevertheless, considers it necessary to clarify
thread is the position of Proletkult, both in the field of organization and in the field
his practical work.

2. Proletkult in its work is the apparatus of the Party in its struggle for
ideological front.

3. Developing its cultural and creative work, Proletkult provides its
strength, experience and achievements in the field of cultural work to trade unions.

4. The relationship between Proletkult and state bodies of Enlightenment is determined
provisions established by general legislation.

5. In order to carry out practical and methodological work, Prolet-
the cult has scientific and methodological departments and commissions, educational and production
educational (demonstrative and service) creative teams, scientific
studios and clubs, clubs and other institutions of the same order, publishing house
issues of theory and practice of Proletkult.

6. Work among the masses is carried out through Trade Unions with the assistance of its charter
update by party officials and by agreeing on the distribution of work
with Political Education, in relation to the already established practice of the Moscow
Proletkult.

7. Plenum, pending clarification of the general financial situation and detailed

new study of the issue of restructuring the work plan, and in connection with this, the bodies

Proletkult in the center and locally considers it inappropriate to convene at this time
moment of the All-Russian Congress. *

MOSCOW PROLETKULT.
CENTRAL STUDIOS OF MOSCOW PROLETKULT.

There are currently two studios: theater and fine arts.”
Due to the reduction in the influx of material resources from outside, the volume of work was
narrowed As a result, by the fall of 1922, the following studios were liquidated: music (choral)
and literary (only methodological centers have been preserved). Necessity of partial:
the transition to self-financing also affected the nature of the work of the retained chairs
due to the educational creative part, the work of production should have been strengthened
natural.

1ST WORKING THEATER AND DIRECTOR'S WORKSHOP.

A new plan for theatrical work was put forward by the Moscow Proletkult
in the spring of 1922 and at the same time approved by the Plenum of the All-Russian Proletkult,
as a desirable “experience”.

The basis was: on the one hand, the principle of using forms so-called.
“small theatrical art” (cabaret, music hall) and circus as the most important forms*
further, subject to their proper elaboration, social impact; on the other hand
Ron, the principle of educating a new actor and director—future organizers
actions not only on the theater stage, but also directly in life (rallies,
processions, festivals, etc.). It is not possible to develop educational work in its entirety.
seemed possible, since the center of attention, by necessity, needed
was to pay attention to the production part. Of the many introduced in the summer of 1922, teachers
methods of teaching (educational practice) are left only: physical education, bio-mechanical
Nika, acrobatics and voice staging. Training comes first
ny moment. The theater group is working hard on the buffoonery"On
“every wise man is satisfied with simplicity,” according to Ostrovsky (free text by S. Third-
Kova, directed by S. Eisenstein). An excerpt from this production (Act 3: “Joffre
going on a hike”) was demonstrated for the first time on April 2 in the Great State
National theater on the day of the anniversary honoring of V. E. Meyerhold. In general, the spec-
The tackle was staged in May on the premises of the Moscow Proletkult. In parallel
with this main work of the 1st Workers' Theater, we worked on: “Prince Hagen”
Sinclair (shown on the premises of the Moscow Proletkult in March 1923) and
“Gas” by Keizer (performances given in the regions). Renewed and shown in areas
also “Lena” comrade. V. Pletneva.

During the period from October 1922 to May 1923, in addition, 40
performances by studio students in 6 districts, at workers' faculties and at the invitation of individual organizations
organizations) with concert programs (including numbers: “Labor”, excerpts from
“The Dawn of Proletkult”, “Strike on the Whites”).

Further works of the 1st Workers' Theater are planned: “Mobile” - Gladkova,
“Gas”—Keizer (remounting), “Prince Hagen” (remounting). Renewed
in a revised form “The Mexican” (dramatization after J. London). Developed-
Scripts for filming are also produced. ; :

sterskikh. In the center, students of Directing Workshops pass together © te-

Russian disciplines in an expanded scope (history of class struggle, scene studies,

CENTRAL CLUB
_ MOSCOW PROLETVULT NAMED AFTER F.I. KALININ.

Moscow Proletkult, together with the MK RKP and MGSPS, organized
Central Club of the Moscow Proletkult named after Fyodor Ivanovich Kalinin.

The tasks of the struggle on the ideological front, the struggle for proletarian culture,
against the bourgeois ideology that is raising its head, are deployed on a very wide scale.
rock front.

In school from its lower classes to higher education, in science, in art: theater,
cinema, literature, fine arts, in extracurricular activities in all its
views, in everyday life, in the Club, everywhere there is still a lot that is far from those
the ideals of communism to which we strive.

With bourgeois ideology, with philistinism, ignorance, the legacy of tsarism
there is a daily struggle to be waged. And you have to be able to fight. We need to study the enemy
study it weake and strong places, you need to forge your weapons, knowledge
theories, practice of new forms of cultural creativity. And it’s not enough, you need to be able to practice
technically in life to build new elements of proletarian class culture, which
Paradise is still in the future.

We are taking our first steps on this path, we are only winning back from the enemy
first positions. And without a long struggle, the bourgeois ideology of its rule
will not yield to us.

And it must be said that, distracted by the combat situation of the civil war,
where issues of life and death of the RSFSR were decided with arms in hand, we did not
could devote enough attention and effort to our ideological front.

At this moment we have the opportunity to begin a systematic struggle in
this area.

We, communists and cultural workers in general, do not yet have a number of
cultural issues, be it in the field of science and especially in art, a distinct
and a clear point of view that can serve as support for every comrade in his
daytime practical work. The work of our communist thought on these
questions, a critical assessment of the practice of our cultural work in all areas
in this practical work, finding new, most fully satisfying
new methods, forms of work, setting up a number of experiments in this area - that’s what
what we need now. You need to concentrate your thoughts somewhere in one place
comrades and their practical achievements, summarize them, generalize mutual
exchange, experience and thoughts to complement each other's work. These goals will be
serve as the “Central Club of the Moscow Proletkult named after Fyodor Ivano-
Vich Kalinin." The attached program of the Club and its charter will indicate to you
How is this Club organized and what is its intended work?

We do not think that the Club will immediately give its comrades all-healing answers in
theory and practice of building proletarian culture, but we express full
confidence that through the collective efforts of comrades, in their close practice
Through technical cooperation in the Club, we will be able to find these answers.

Members of the Club may be members of the RCP on the recommendation of the district committee, members
Profsoycall on the recommendation of the provincial department of their Union, Proletcultists
on the recommendation of the Presidium of Proletkult or the same comrades on the recommendation
3 Club members. In the latter case, the Board reserves the right to
No. 8 ROTE lLT. 247

get additional recommendations from individual comrades above
organizations.

WHAT KIND OF THEATER DOES THE WORKING CLASS NEED.
Protocol of the report at the Central Club of the Moscow Proletkult 19/X1-22.

The speaker Comrade Arvatov develops the problem of the proletarian theater from two points
vision, namely; 1) takes the theater as one of the moments of construction in the plan
measured socialist society, and 2) approaches the problem from the point of view
using existing forms of theatre.

The starting point is the definition of theatrical art as
creativity in the field of organizing human actions.

In a bourgeois society, which is not systematically organized at its core,
the urgent need was the illusory organization of everyday life, the replenishmentreal anarchist life in the imagination and with the help of the imagination. This is
was the social function of the theater, which in the era of commodity economy became a “special
Noah" ry. :

the opposite of bourgeois society, the working class, in its own way,
trends, is called upon to build a unified, systematic collectivist society
No. 8 PROLETKULT. 251

in which, as Marx put it, all illusions will disappear. Can't be in
in such a society there is room for illusory art (the task of the proletariat is not to depict
destroy reality, but organize it, change it).

What to do now? Destroy the theater? No,” the speaker answers. “Theater.”
can be used in two directions. It is necessary, on the one hand, to go
to make the means of educating an actor the means of educating a
every person. It is necessary to open a number of laboratories that would engage in experimental
resolution of the question of human organization not only in terms of aesthetics,
chesically (Comrade Meyerhold was the first to take this path with his experiences in organizing
theatrical movement based on physical education). On the other hand, you need to use
call theater for politics! struggle, economic, etc. While humanity
is still floundering in diapers, while it is still necessary to act in the “way”—the theater is necessary
use as a form of influence. Here the question arises in all its severity:
which of the theatrical forms are the forms of the greatest in real
conditions of social influence. The speaker considers these forms to be forms
“cabaret type, music hall, farce theater, circus, i.e. forms that go
into the masses, bursting into everyday life, and not calling for contemplation—forms, devoid of
ny illusions and establishing the greatest degree of communication between the actor and the viewer.
One should not be afraid of the “low quality” of these forms. Division of arts into high ones
and low fetish. Everything can be used by the proletariat for its purposes.

Comrade Arvatov summarizes his report in the following terms: 1) gap
with an easel theater; 2) liquidation of the theater and replacement of human organization with
theater organizationcenturies in life; 3) laboratory work on a person
and material; 4) use of existing theatrical forms, forms not
leading away from life, but rushing into it.

The co-rapporteur on the issue of the proletarian theater was Comrade. Pletnev.

Modern theater does not meet the requirements that it imposes
revolution. Three reasons determine this: 1) the emptiness of the theater,
powerless to reveal the intensity of the emotional element that was
the result of the revolution, 2) unpreparedness in social terms of man-
ical material in the old theater and 3) formal conservatism. Main,
Comrade Pletnev sees the initial task of theatrical work in creating a repertoire
macaw The quests of writers must be placed in inextricable connection with the quests
theater studios: the method of separating the actor, director and author should be
rejected. The life of the revolution in its extraordinary sustained heroism, the moment
romantic and satirical—these are the three main directions in which
work may begin to create a repertoire.

Without denying the importance of flexible, fast forms of theatrical action, Comrade Pletnev
does not agree, however, with Comrade Arvatov in ‘his statement about/ the possibility of limiting
be limited to such forms only. Grandiose ideas of the revolution, says
Comrade Pletnev, - cannot be expressed in such quickly flashing forms.
We cannot do without a theater of great action, without a monumental theatre. X.

In the debate that opened after the reports, comrade objected. Arvatov T. T. Kozlov,
Diament, Volin and others. Comrade. Kozlov puts forward the point of view that the search for
tariat in the field of art must inevitably have as their starting point
reality, everyday life Art is an organizing moment because
an artist knows how to see and reproduce ‘what others don’t see. Decadence,
futurism - everything innovative was brought to us from the West, as decadent, to impose
The proletariat cannot tolerate this decadence.

Against the slogan about the use of “cabaret” forms to create pro-
Tara Theater objects to T. 'Diament'. If in a café-chantan the bourgeoisie is “steaming”

", then you cannot wish the same for the worker. In general, the proletarian theater
will arise spontaneously from the bottom of the proletarian masses.
253 i No. 8

Comrade Volin points out the need to give in the theater, on the one hand,
revolutionary life, on the other hand, the romanticism that permeates our
revolution

The speaker's point of view was supported by Comrades Gamza, Kravchunovsky and Brik.
Comrade Chuzhak makes several adjustments to it.

Comrade Gamza—emphasizes that Comrade Arvatov takes art as an organi-
a beginning, as a moment of construction (art is not a mirror, but a hammer). If
the art of the past was what ten people did, and thousands
stared at them, then in the art of the future the basic principle should be
not “gazing”, but the creativity of life. An actor must stop being only an artist
com of the stage, he must become an artist-citizen. The meaning of leftist currents
in art lies precisely in the fact that old forms are broken and preparations
provides the basis for the flourishing of art in a socialist society. Just like
just as Marx, the child of bourgeois science, cost his mother the death, in the same way
and futurism, the child of bourgeois art, will cost its mother the death.

Comrade Kravchunovsky speaks about the forms of agitation and propaganda theater,
sharing the view of Comrade Arvatov and considering the forms indicated by the speaker
forms of the greatest, in current conditions, social impact.

According to Comrade Brik, the task of reflecting everyday life cannot be a task of prose-
Tariat. The proletariat needs a spectacle where it can see, without any deception,
demonstration of human dexterity and strength. Therefore, those who
offers forms of circus, café chantana (?). Many people talk about this kind of indecency
art, but can’t “dating” houses, for example, be turned into proletarian ones?
dorms? The same is true with cafes. This form can be used
to call for proletarian purposes. As for the everyday theater, this theater is Comrade Brik
characterizes it as complete hypocrisy. No onee will go look at the barricades
in the theater, if he himself was at the barricades.

The last of the comrades who spoke, Comrade Tretyakov, expressed that
the sense that the theater must inevitably make a revolution within itself. Change
If industrial relations have changed, the psyche cannot remain unchanged. From
changes in forms, while, of course, not going anywhere. And those forms that are intended
What we are looking for now is precisely the forms of organization of living human material.

There was no final word from Comrade Arvatov, due to his illness.

0 THE SERAPION BROTHERS AND LITERATURE IN GENERAL.
Report-debate at the Central Club of the Moscow Proletkult on February 6, 1923.

The starting point for the speaker, Comrade. Kogan, is the reason

exciting thoughts lie outside the field of lyricism, and are characteristic of the present moment
This is the death of lyric poetry and the revival of fiction. Three main

FUTURIS M.

Protocol of the report-debate at the Central Club of the Moscow Proletkult
March 3, 1923.

Comrade Brik begins his report by pointing out that critics of futurism
they usually use the material indifferently, no matter what kind of futurism it is
related. Meanwhile, futurism during its existence. had several
stages of development and this cannot be ignored. First of all, one cannot help but know that
There is Italian futurism and Russian futurism. The difference between them
huge. Italian futurism is imperialist, Russian futurism is revolutionary. War
was proclaimed by Italian Futurism as the hygiene of the world. In his Mani-
feste Marinetti said: we will sing the praises of cities shaken by crowds
workers, we will sing of anarchist rebellion, but at the same time we will
glorify war. Marinetti's idea was correct in the sense that the explosion with that
or the other side was bound to ‘happen. The whole point, however, is
that the Italian futurists were closer to war, because they were children

Y
254 from No. 8

ruling class, their iceology was the ideology of the bourgeois, imperial
listical, Therefore, there is nothing surprising in the fact that now Italian
futurists are on the side of the fascists.

As for Russian futurism, it did not grow out of Italian or ideological
logically or organizationally. Russian futurism arose independently of the Italian
sky. Lachey in 1914 Marinetti tried to contact Russian Futurism, but
to no avail. Characterizing the first futuristic groups in Russia,
Comrade Brik notes that initially Russian futurism resulted mainly in
in laboratory work on words. That group, however, which published in 1914
“Collection of Futurists” carried through the entire war trends that were opposite
imperialist tendencies of Italian futurismma. A huge role in the group
played in the celebration and design of futurism in Russia. 1917 Those of the futurists
who even before that time had taken the city and modernity as their themes—understood
17 year as “realization of possibilities”. The destruction of the past became for them
now not destruction for the sake of destruction, but destruction for that new
construction, which the proletariat began. For this group of futurists
social. the goal was clear. Another group reacted differently to October:
Let it be October, but this does not concern us, only laboratory work is important. This
c-^ group fell away from the first, united at the present time under the sign
“Lef”: All those who did not see the social revolution have disappeared. This is where everyone came from
branches: imagists, nichevoki, etc. As for the “Lef” group, it is pre-
its creators consider themselves not creators in general, but makers of a certain art
art, that art that leads to the goals outlined by the proletariat. Accept
agitation art and art entering into production and everyday life are toil. At the same time,
The Lef group believes that you cannot build the future without completely rejecting the old.
This is her significant difference from her fellow proletarian writers who are still
under the spell of old forms.

After Comrade Brik’s report, the poets perform < reading their works:
Aseev, Kruchenykh, Mayakovsky.

The speaker, Comrade Skachko, proceeds from the recognition of the need to take into account the psycho-
logic of that mass, in the midst of which it is necessary to draw the line of proletarian ideology
gical front. In literature, as one of the sections of this front, it is necessary
find a form of influence on the mass reader that would teach him
to reading, interested and aroused those feelings, without which, although
knowledge of the ideas of the proletarian revolution is possible, but there are no conditions for action °
in accordance with these ideas. The form of such influence on the mass reader
t. Skachko believes the so-called. tabloid novel, the distinctive features of which are
are contained in dynamism, simplicity and richness of content, romanticism,
intense heroism and, as a result of all this, extreme entertainment.

Having settled on a chivalric adventure novel as a starting point
tabloid novel, comrade. jumps overfurther to the characteristics of the novels
in the bourgeois era, when, with the final establishment of the bourgeoisie, for the first time
the “psychological novel” is moving into place, and the adventure novel is being pushed aside
into the background, sinks and becomes coarser, nevertheless continuing to retain those
features that made it a fascinating read. For various cars
These are the basic features that make a pulp novel entertaining,
of course, are modified: for example, Victor’Hugo and Eugene-Sue have an interesting

characters to whom the reader's sympathies are attached, In English

in this literary form, the struggle against absolutism and religion, against the monarchy

stic class and bourgeois society. The example of Jack London proves

forms.

ART AND PRODUCTION.
Protocol of the report at the Central Club of MoscowProletkult March 27, 1923.

The speaker, Comrade Arvatov, raises the question of how to connect
artistic creativity with the production process. In this area the struggle
is now between two main groups: defenders of artisanal art and
defenders of industrial art. The first claim that artisanal production
production, which in the past was closely associated with artistic creativity, has not died
and now that an artist can create only when he is free and not subject to
repaired to the machine, and what can be used, therefore, can only be that industry
production, which is individual, i.e., handicraft industry. this point
point of view, the speaker characterizes it as undoubtedly idealistic, does not admit-
giving rise to the possibility that the walker could work not individually. Line
further development of production lies along the path of industrial development
production, If we introduce art into handicraft industry, then
art itself will not enter into everyday life. From this angle, support for artisanal
production *is a clearly reactionary action. Defenders of artisanal art
states also point to the enormous importance of the handicraft industry, as
export item, but even here it is necessary to keep in mind that long-term use
The development of this export item is doomed to failure, since old stocks will be
are depleted, but there will be no significant influx of new items, due to the non-mass
handicraft production. Finally, one cannot ignore the fact that
that there is demand for our handicrafts abroad only among the bourgeoisie,
and this demand is due mainly to the interest in these products as “ra-
rites." Count on buyers among the working class, peasants and townspeople
you can’t: they won’t buy things they don’t need. Without a doubt, he continues.
speaker, that at present we can only talk about the entry of art
into large industrial production. And here we are talking about methods when
what are the two main points of view?nia. One is put forward by supporters of the
masonry art, the other - defenders of artistic engineering. First point
vision is sufficiently known: the artist “gives” things beautiful forms,
the artist, taking the finished product, decorates it externally. Fundamentally applied
new art is the same “pure” art: it assumes the possibility

MOSCOW PROLETKULT IN TRADE UNION CLUBS.

Club work of the Moscow Proletkult in the past winter of 1922-23
flowed under completely unusual conditions: Proletkult did not have a single
“your” club, i.e. one that would be supplied at his expense completely or at least
would be in terms of teacher pay, as was the case in past years.

By agreement with K.O. MGSPS, Proletkult was supposed to manage the work
that in separate clubs of various Trade Unions. Organizationally, these clubs are sub-
were carried out by K. O. Soyuzov, although a certain part of the organizational influence, according to
It seems that it belonged to Prolstkult. But over time, as
The trade unions managed to strengthen the material base of the club, they are increasingly
clubs, instructed by Prolet-
cult (they appointed a manager, redrawn estimates and staffing and gave instructions -
proposals to the manager, without coordinating them with Proletkult) Moreover, they de-
Attempts were made to interfere in the cultural work of these clubs. Such aspirations
The cultural departments and the generally abnormal situation of Proletkult further complicated
The already difficult task of managing work in other people's clubs. As a result, the club
This season’s work has yielded much less results than it could have
give with the forces and resources that Proletkult spent on it.

In the fall of 1922, Proletkult supervised the work of more than 20 clubs.
To implement this leadership, Proletkult supplied the clubs with instructors,
who worked according to the plan and programs of Proletkult, checked and instructed
teachers available locally, organized regular teaching meetings
givers on questions of methodology and practice toLubricant work. For club heads
Bami organized a seminary using the method of club work. However, experience
said that such instruction is enough to keep the club working
at a certain average level. In order to raise it significantly
nogo height, constant supervision and supervision of work on site is necessary.
The absence of proletkult workers on the ground due to the organizational non-
ry mentioned above led to a weakening of the clubs’ connection with
1roletcult, especially when the work of the clubs has already improved. Then Pro-
letkult switched to a different system of instruction, attaching a club to each
responsible instructor, In total, there were 8 clubs covered: Club
at the 1st Model Printing House, Central Printers Club, Simonovsky
Club "Labor and Creativity", United No.: Podolsk Plants, United
Bakers Club, Shzeynikov Club, Club named after. Zilina (formerly Prosthetic Plant),
Club d. im. Kalyaeva; relations with other clubs remained
the former ones. On these 8 clubs you can trace the line that was drawn
Preletkult in club work,

The main task of the club’s work over the past winter was: to install new
forms of mass work that would make it possible to move from organizational
dedicated to propaganda work among the masses. This resulted in a number of very significant
particular tasks, such as: 1) establishing close interaction between mass and
circle work; 2) the restructuring of the circle appropriate for this purpose
work; 3) gradual transfer of the center of gravity of club work < artistic
to scientific or at least establishing some balance between these
two types.

The revolution in club work began with an attack on the most fortified
her position is art circles. At the beginning of autumn, there was a permanent situation in all clubs.
The question of the work of circles according to the plan of a unified art studio has been raised. Main
The principle of a single studio is that club clubs do not work for
reaching the depths of art, andfor the production of certain club work.
Hence, the content of all work must be consistent with the objectives of the club. Next,
It is recognized that there are no separate circles: music, drama
it. d., there is a single art studio divided into sections. Members of all
circles are united on a number of common subjects, and all circles are united on common
tasks. The job of the Drama Studio is therefore to produce the repertoire.
The literary studio publishes a newspaper and compiles scripts. Art makes posters, billboards, etc. d.
Muzo participates in productions, etc. If we remember the usual work of drama
studios, the main goal of which was to learn to be an actor, then then a priest.
the intensity with which music studios studied their art, the pictures that
were drawn in the Iso studio, it will become clear which wall had to be broken through
Proletkult in this one of the most essential parts of club work. In the clubs
who worked under the leadership of Proletkult for the second or even third year,
the restructuring of the artistic work was relatively easy, since they were already
prepared for it by all previous work. From the principles of a single studio
first of all, the new content of the work and the unification of all
studios for general productions; the situation was much more difficult with the introduction of general
for all students of compulsory subjects (physical education, choral singing, rhythmics,
as well as a number of socio-political subjects).

The Club takes first place in implementing the principles of a unified studio
1st Model Printing House. The drama studio of this Club was always working on
propaganda repertoire. The Studios available at the Club worked with her:
Art, Choral, Orchestra. He was brought in to stage the Komsomol Easter
and scientific circle. The studio staged a number of charades, dramatizations, ditties and
small plays. Of the latter, “The Shadow of Karl Liebknecht” is especially interesting, in
the action of which the Studio introduced cinematography. The studio has been operating for 2 years and has
such skill that some productions are staged independently, without a director.
sulfur EThis is also facilitated by the fact that over the years the studio members have greatly advanced in
political development. It is especially interesting to trace the evolution that
I did Studio Izo in this club. This studio was built very conservatively
in matters of art and, even worse, she was very apolitical; The club as a whole
she was not interested, did not want to help him. A series of conversations held with her—
on the one hand, and most importantly, constant involvement in general productions, on the other,
led to the fact that by the end of the year they enthusiastically, regardless of time,
worked for the Club, made scenery for revolutionary productions, decorated
Club it. d. They had to work on posters and playbills, and gradually
There was a significant shift in their views on art. Regarding the merger
all Studios in general classes, then so far we have managed to make it mandatory for everyone
only political literacy and physical education.

PROLET CULTS ON THE SITE.
TVERSKY PROLETKULT.

The Tver Proletkult was a provincial center for about five years, uniting
reaching up to five district Proletkults, but due to different conditions (lack of
funds, experienced leaders) district Proletkults ceased to exist.
Some of them had valuable achievements: for example, in the field of art—Torzhok
(choir), staged and performed by the Scientific Studio (Rzhev).

Tver Proletkult has Studios: Teo, Iso, Lit-krug, Muzo - according to class. pianos,
domra, choir classes, physical education (compulsory subject for everyone) and club courses
nal trainee instructors, general and specialist area managers
clubs, circles.

In Studios and Courses, along with the study of special issues
art—general education and political education are seriously
naya work. The following were introduced as compulsory subjects: 1) basic issues of political science;
spendthrifts, owls construction, 2) political economy in connection with the history of culture, 3) historical
ical materialism, 4) history of the labor movement in Russia and the West, 5) historical
ria social teachings, 6) world economy and capitalism, 7) current situation
world economy and in the RSFSR, 8) linguistics, Russian language, 9) mathematics,
10) world studies (synthetic course: chemistry, physics, zoology, anatomy, biology
it. d.), 11) study of labor, the ABC of labor, acquaintance with crafts, with production.

The studios are built according to the principle of the Unified Studio of the Moscow Proletkult,
communicate about their achievements, partly mutually study the areas of their production
Vodstvo Over the past season, the work of Theo-studio, which made 36
steps in different areas of the city. Theo's repertoire included: “Mexican”, “Three
Jesus"“Labor”, “Uprising” (Republished “The Agony of the World”, “Tsar-Hunger”
(reworking of Andreev’s play), “Among the Flames” (after P. M. Kerzhentsev), “May”
(propaganda, parody of the “United Capitalist Front”), coll. recitation, etc.

Proletkult's performances are marked with the local press, reporting performances -
Lito, Theo, Muzo, and part of the Izo exhibition deserved gratitude from Lips. Congress
The trade unions for which these performances were organized.

The domra orchestra also carried out maintenance work (13 performances during the season)
and at the same time studied folk songs, foreign musical works
denies, transcribed into sheet music for orchestra of works by proletarian poets.

During the season, the 2nd group, domra, was prepared for performances, the general composition of the orchestra
ste 30 people; performances are popular in working-class and urban areas

believe. )

The art studio works under the guidance of a constructivist artist, but studies
all directions are technical, without assigning one or another bias. Bli-
The most practical goal (partly there are implementations) is a poster, decorative
art, illustration, popular print, cartoon, slogans, modeling.

The literary circle has only been organized for two months, about 35 works have been sorted out,
accepted 20, work is carried out exclusively through creative and critical means, -
Part of the study is correspondence, stylistics, journalism, methods of the proletarian
sky art criticism, a collection is being prepared.

Club Courses will finish by June 10-15, and cadets will be assigned
we to local clubs in order to provide methodological guidance to the work of the circles.

IVANOVO-VOZNESENSKY. PROLETKULT.

In recent months—February-May—the work has expanded. Arrival in February
lecturers and workers from the center pushed the work that was frozen. Remaining
two Studios Iso and Teo, with a predominantly social composition of workers (mostly
most members of the RCP and RKSM), earned more intensively, with a surge of new strength and
materials from the center.

Theater Studio, with a change of director and addition to the work program
lectures on Marxist analysis of the most important moments in the history of art and theater,
came to life. Preparations for Komsomol Easter began in mid-March. Were taken
into the work of the play “Neporzach” by S. Tretyakov and “The Resurrection of Christ”, written
on the spot, on the instructions of the RKP Ukom for holding Komsomol Easter, one of
Proletkult workers. At the same time, by the day (the Lena events were resumed)
Pletnev’s play “Lena” was presented. In order to work on studying acting technique
and elaboration of propaganda methods (in terms of work in an open area)
theaters were worked on and at the end of March 2 propaganda films were staged
on the topics of the day: 1) Fascism, 2) Ruhr. They were accompanied by a prologue-clownery, accompanied by
driven by the work of the acrobatic group. These two productions of Fascism-Ruhr, unfortunately
nia, could not be given according to the planned plan, because: a) there were no funds
to sew original costumes and had to use existing ones, from
why the production suffered greatly, 6) there were no funds and sufficient preparation
from the Izo studio to develop the set design planned by the director, -
they played in cloth, and where there was none, on a bare stage and a simple machine-stool
penalties. Despite all these defects, both plays were well received internationally.
stakh and were staged at the Soviet Theater in Ivanovo, in the 2 largest workers
clubs in Ivanovo and 6 workers' clubs in the districts.

VLADIMIR DMITRIEVICH BUZIN.

He was a staunch fighter on the political and cultural front.

As a member of the RCP, he firmly believed in the working class and its triumph,
and, striving to achieve the latter, he devotes all his strength to awaken more
unconscious workers, to instill in them confidence in themselves and their purpose. Thanks to him
energy, the party was replenished with perhaps more than a dozen conscious members
new RKP and RKSM.

He spent his short life in struggle and work. The son of a worker, he
did not have the opportunity to receive an education, but, thanks to natural gifts,
He managed to educate himself and throughout his work he expanded his knowledge. Up to 17 years old
he worked in workers' circles in Moscow on | ›lighting workers, but his work
did not satisfy within limited limits. . After the October Revolution he became
a member of the RCP and threw himself into work with all his energy and enthusiasm; worked
among the railway workers of the Kursk region, with his participation in the Bauman region
There was a Workers' Club named after Kalyaev.

early 1920 comrade. Buzin ends up in the Urals (Ekaterinburg). He is happy
I realized that I was in an industrial area where you canbring back cultural work
among the workers who had recently freed themselves from Kolchak’s whip. He refused
from the personal “I”, forgot about the family and completely went into work. And, despite the overload
the importance of working at the Headquarters of the Eastern District of Vsevobuch, where he did a lot of work,
combining several responsibilities for lack of employees, comrade. Buzin accepted
enthusiastic participation in the organization of Proletkult. Soon he was released from Headquarters
completely and switched to Proletkult work, where, also for lack of
employees, in addition to secretarial duties, performed various duties. Despite
to the difficult financial situation of 20-21, despite all the blows and
greedy for Proletkult, even from party comrades, comrade. Elderberry firmly
supports the spirit of comrades who are ready to quit their jobs and give up.

During his work at Proletkult, he organized several studios, where
only workers were accepted and the proletkult program was carried out, and where
The instructors worked under his leadership. He himself ran all day long
to the Party, made reports, worked in Proletkult, conducted
conversations, and in the evening he studied at the Drama Studio at the Zhel.-Dor Club. named after Voyner.
The composition here was exclusively working, advanced. Comrade Buzin was in this
Studio for everyone: both the teacher, and when, with his intense work, it was possible from this
Studios to open the 1st Workers' Theater in the Urals, director, decorator, prop maker.
lecturer, musician, playwright and actor. It was kind of relentless
a mechanism that works 20 hours a day. }

But, already working in a production position, Comrade. Buzin didn’t look away
from life; he was aware of everything, tried to instill attentiveness in his comrades
to life and instill proletarian class consciousness. His constant words:
“Comrades, there is no need to break away from those from whom you came, but you came from the heart
worker; Working in the theater, we must always be on our guard; if we need it
go to the factory, plant, we will go; If we need to go to the front, let’s take rifles and let’s go!”
And with his fiery words he lit up the graydza workers; they firmly believed
into him and his words, and the words reached their goal, not a single cleanup worker of the Studio
missed, all campaigns and events in the RSFSR were noted by the Studio. Thankfully
By giving this, Proletkult won sympathy among the workers, and the workers' Unions
in difficult moments for Proletkult they are its support. But Comrade Buzin led
and political work: along with work in Proletkult, he has all the responsibilities
party and active member of the RCP. }

#5
No. 8 PROLETKULT. 269

In the summer of 1922, the Workers' Theater headed by Comrade. Buzin worked in “Houses”
Rest" Trade Unions; in addition to his duties at the Theater, comrade. Buzin led the cultural
educational work among vacationing workers, who limitlessly
loved as a comrade, a friend, loved for his humor, which did not leave him until
last days. Small, a little lame, he rolls in quickly like a ball
in the midst of workers who joyfully greet him; a conversation begins about the current
moment; a lot of questions, but comrade. Buzin skillfully answers everything, and, listening to him,
the workers are inspired, their eyes sparkle, they greedily hang on every word. Conversation
ends with noise: “Volodya, tell me more.” “Yes, Comrade Buzin, tell me more!” He
tired, but continues; after finishing, the workers accompany him home and again
endlessly asking questions.

At the end of June he falls ill with typhus. Already sick, he takes part in the play
le, in a comic role; the next day he is taken to the hospital, where
8 days later—July 6, 1922—he dies, being only 24 years old, irreplaceable
a worker among the working class and Proletkult, a faithful worker of the RCP.

M.M.

ALEXANDER IVANOVICH ZUGRIN.

I met Alexander Ivanovich Zugrin in 1919, at the beginning
September, upon my arrival from Ukraine. A.I. just arrived before
at the Moscow Proletkult as a studio artist. It was a young man of about 19, walking
in a blouse, in army boots, in a cap, from under which came reddish
hair. The face is pale and thin, the eyes are thoughtful and focused.

V.I. quickly gained sympathy among us,studio people - we loved him.
He spoke little about himself, but from the few words he shared, it is clear
It turned out that his life was not very good.

Before entering Proletkult, he had just arrived from Nizhny Novgorod.
Novgorod, where the older brother worked in a factory transferred to Moscow; with him
his family also lived there. In Nizhny A.I. it was necessary to unload and load wagons,
clear streets and clear snow from roofs. If he ever got started
money, his first duty was to buy paper, pencil and paint, and in his free time
spent time drawing or writing sketches.

A. I. fell in love with painting since school. While in Petrograd,
he joined the photographer as an apprentice retoucher, but this job was not for him
to his liking, he wanted to go to art school. But how was it
tsarist government, the son of a worker or peasant gets into a government educational institution
institution, especially without artistic training and tuition fees, and
also for livelihood? In Petrograd, A.I. goes to metal
factory, first as a student, then as an apprentice turner; in the evening he goes to draw
To “encourage the arts,” and on holidays he works or writes sketches. Of the few
sketches and drawings that A.I. preserved from his moves from Petrograd to Nizhny,
from Nizhny to Moscow, most impressed me: a sketch of a windmill
mills and outskirts. Petrograd. At Proletkult he was interested in left-wing painting.
The instructors took him seriously for his hard work and perseverance. Self-image
A.I. studied a lot, bought and borrowed books from the library, more and more
related to art. 1920 was the most difficult year; some walked like shadows
for a month or more they did not eat bread, but ate only frozen potatoes.
Zugrin spoke little about himself, how he lived and ate at that time. He's bigger
he was most worried when he had no paints or linoleum, nothing with which to cut
cliche.

; 96 rbe y ke? oh my god

In the summer of 1920, A.I. wrote a poster—children’s clubs—for an exhibition in
Polytechnic Museum. I saw this pLakat, and I was amazed how much love

INHUN.
(Institute of Artistic Culture).

INHUK is officially a scientific society uniting masters of left
art, its peculiarity, which distinguishes it from a number of other similar societies,
is that it is a creative organization par excellence, where
ideology of artistic consciousness. :

In ideological terms, the work of INKHUK can be divided into two headings:
on the one hand, the recognition of easel forms as not meeting the needs of the revolution
tion today, and on the other hand, the development of the idea of production art, as
ideas conditioned by the entire dialectic of development of economic and political
and in connection with the active social role performed by the proletariat.

In practical terms, the work of INHUK has two main lines: constructivism
and production start.

One of the last tasks facing INHUK is the preparation of a series of
publications that should cover both the practical work of its members and
and the ideological platform as a whole.

N. T—in.

VKHUTEMAS.
(Higher Artistic and Technical Workshops).

It is difficult to find another institution that, in such a relatively short
time would have been able to do so many times, and almost everytimes fundamentally,
reorganize.

All these reforms and reorganizations, by the way, are always happening
with great noise, created a special popularity in the artistic circles of VKHUTEMAS
polarity; this popularity developed as a result of long and stubborn battles, which
active workers of VKHUTEMAS had to endure, - first of all,
mainly to communist students, in the struggle for revolutionary
establishing an art school, for cleansing the school of scholasticism in the struggle
against apoliticality, “autonomy”, etc. d., it, d.

The main thing is about the work on the merits.

It ultimately boiled down to the transformation of science and art from
means of enslavement into a means of emancipation of the working masses.

Since the old royal school was a citadel and ideological
and practical reaction, this school had to be destroyed. It was impossible
however, to do this simply by closing the school: it was impossible to stop the reproduction
production of skilled labor, it was necessary to organize
a school that corresponds to the new content in its methods of work. Next—
the school could not fulfill its purpose if its composition did not change,
i.e. proletarianization would not have been fully carried out. / finally, from what
the old school, in the person of even its best representatives, waved it off in every possible way,
this is the connection between the school and the specific conditions of production.

Chronologically, these paths were carried out at VKHUTEMAS in this order. First
the blow was directed towards the destruction of the old school, the point of departure

18
274 ge No. No. 8

this period—Intercity (Moscow, St. Petersburg) Conference of art students
ny schools and studios, which existed in April 1918. Many higher educational institutions
at that time they were entirely or almost entirely on the other side of the barricade. That
that art school students ended up on this side is explained by the fact that
It was relatively affordable to enroll in these schools; the low fees attracted
here are the poorest elements of the working intelligentsia and office workers. Half the lineup
the conference fell on theprivate schools and studios with evening classes and
an even cheaper board, therefore even more affordable.

This conference developed a new type of art school called
nium of the State Free Workshops.

Freedom was understood as, firstly, free access for students, and secondly
attracting artists unrecognized by the old government and, thirdly, freedom
teaching. In fact, this resulted in “freedom from teaching,” but this
conferences could not be foreseen.

At the conference there was a split with the students of the Academy of Arts, who
left the conference.

After this conference, the entire RSFSR was overcome by a spontaneous desire to open
State Free Workshops - they open in almost every
volosts; There were also those in which there were no students, but ‘there were only
drivers.

A positive feature of Free Workshops. was that, having opened a free
access to schools, they made it possible for workers and employees to enter there;
thus the Workshops became proletarianized.

In Moscow, instead of the Stroganov School, the 1st Free
Workshops; instead of the School of Painting, Sculpture and Architecture - 1st Free
Workshops. .

Although the leaders in both the 1st and 2nd Workshops were almost the same,
However, in terms of the composition of students, the I-e Workshops turned out to be more radical. Summer
1919, a co-organized cell of the RCP, with a part grouped around it
proletarian students, begins to openly “interfere” in school affairs.

In general, the VKHUTEMAS students had an exceptional role: all
these orientations towards artistic youth on the part of the central authorities are essentially
were oriented towards a large, strong and united force of organized
students; in fact, the students through their organized opinion
could influence the artistic policy not only of his school, but also of
tough politics in general.

At that time it was already clear that the Free Workshops were fulfilling their
positive role in the sense of destroying the old school, and that it is time to takethere is
for organizing a new school. Meanwhile, program-free Free Workshops
were not such a school, especially since all management was in the hands of the
horny bureaucracy.

And now the cell more precisely formulates its requirements for the school, namely:
1) there can be no school without a program, 2) down with the counter-revolutionary profession
sura, 3) transfer the management of the school into the hands of the students. In 1st Workshop cells
there was no, but the student executive committee (the active part of the headman), at least
strongly supported the cell's demand.

Despite persistent and categorical demands, the Iso department
no efforts were made to improve school work. Then the cell starts
as a last resort - declares the Council of Workshops dissolved and, in the person of its
representatives, occupies its premises.

At the beginning of 20, the executive committee of the 1st Workshops again raised the question of the need
the ability to develop a program and organize student participation
in management.

Finally, the Art Department convened in June 1920 the All-Russian Conf.
Rent of teachers and students of Art workshops. The Conference adopted a resolution
update: schools must have programs with a laboratory teaching method;
schools should be divided into higher and secondary; students are allowed to
all organs on a parity basis; merge { and And Moscow Workshops.

This is where the history of VKHUTEMAS begins in its proper sense.

A program is being developed by the notorious artistic and scientific disciplines"
us. Little by little communists returning from the front and those remaining active
workers begin work on organizing students, a frenzied
campaign for disciplines, the best forces of young professors are attracted here
and students sent from the province. VKHUTEMAS is experiencing an absolute re-
population, the cell begins to campaign for the organization of the Worker
Faculty. In the fall of 1920, the Workers' Faculty was opened.

The organization of the Workers' Faculty takes a lot of effort from the active part of the workers,
have to work on several fros at oncentov, and failure in one place could
would undo all the work.

At the beginning of 1921, the organizational successes of VKHUTEMAS were clearly determined.
VKHUTEMAS very quickly and successfully coped with the onslaught of the old professoriate, leaving
outside the school, which tried to blow up VKHUTEMAS from the inside, organizing
a small part of the unlucky, confused students.

This attack further united both the students and the leg that went with them
in step with the “young” professor. .

VKHUTEMAS has not achieved complete organizational success to this day:
Along with workshops that have both programs and methods, there are quite a few
the quality of “dark corners” where the revolutionary broom has not visited. In the majority
cases, these places are under the protection of the Almighty and are safely
are wary of any revolutionization.

The development of a large campaign dates back to the same time, the beginning of 21
for production faculties.

The production faculties of VKHUTEMAS ‘a, although they were included in its countless
schemes, but in fact it was all on paper.

In incredibly difficult conditions, among thousands of hardships, in the complete absence
material resources, work begins on equipping faculties with the necessary
smoking machines and recycling in relation to this training programs.

Again, here the initiative comes from the student executive committee, which started
processing of one's own professorship and then a wide campaign for training
directly at the production itself, agitation among students for the necessary
consumption of ITPI in production. The results of this work should ultimately
were to provide a specialist trained for a specific area of production, for
a certain stage of its development, i.e. in fact, this would establish inextricability
a new connection between school and life; students would be trained in two ways
main lines: 1) studying the subject according to the latest word in science and art
quality and 2) its application in specific production.

Although VKHUTEMAS has achieved some results in terms of equipment, everything
there is still more to come in this areaIt's a huge job. This is a device
and school methods to modern concrete production and will be the closest
the focal point of the work of VKHUTEMAS.

This note does not allow us to dwell on the influence that
VKHUTEMAS provided assistance to other schools in the province. In general, VHUT EMAS
was a kind of magnetic beacon that illuminated the path around itself far away,
and attracted the strongest elements of the student body.

THEATER-WORKSHOP OF VSEVOLOD MEYERHOLD.

Theater of Vsevolod Meyerhold (I mean not only the theater, formally
bearing this name since the end of 1922, but also the entire work of Vs. Um. Meyerhold
in the premises of theater 6. Zone for 1920-1923) is defined as the first, revolutionary
tionizing the form of theatrical action based on an active struggle for
social revolution. From “Zor” (7/X1-1920) and (“Mysteries-Buff” (IU 1921)
theater Sun. Meyerhold came to “The Magnanimous Cuckold” (25L\U 1922),
who made a formal revolution in modern theater. This performance is
a product of GVYTM'a's laboratory work (about GVYTM*e further). first practical
using biomechanics—a system of stage movements that reveal health
a new construction of man, strengthened by physical culture. In "Great"
stuffy Cuckold” refusal to reproduce “vital”—in fact, inorganic
called-movements, rejection of arbitrary invention of movements and affirmation
simple, schematized and at the same time the most expressive movements
in full compliance with their stage assignments. Regarding things on stage—-
rejection of figurativeness, affirmation of the utility of material design
scenes: a three-dimensional installation, each part of which performs specific
functions in the play (model of the design of GVYTM student V. Lyutse, corrected
bathed then by L.S. Popova). The director's interpretation is extremely original:
the psychological, even psychopathic plot of the play Krommlanka is neutralized
the most effective and p form of staging Sun. Meyerhold.

FollowingThe final production by V. E. Meyerhold - “The Death of Tarelkin” (24/X! - 1922)
- in terms of folk farce. Installations similar to the design of the Magnanimous
“Cuckold”, not on stage: instead of it, furniture (work by V.F. Stepanova), again
schematic and constructed with a tendency towards its greatest use in
acting. Sukhovo-Kobylin's play is interpreted in terms of bright grotesque.

The last production of the last season—“The Earth on End” (4/—1923)—
M. Martinet’s play “Night”, remade by S. M. Tretyakov. Reworking of the play
was caused by an abundance of rhetoric and a lack of expressiveness in the text. There were
large bills were made; the remaining text was rearranged: deleted
unnecessary words, in many phrases the words were rearranged so that the text became
compressed and percussive. Household items were thrown away; action takes place
in modernity, abstracted from the locality. And here is a peculiar interpretation:
the anti-militarist plot retained its character in terms of agitation against
bourgeois militarism, but, at the same time, the form of the production puts forward a military
organization as the most harmonious organization of human groups.
No wonder the director’s work is Vs. Meyerhold is dedicated to “The Red Army and Per-
to the first Red Army soldier of the RSFSR Leon Trotsky." “The Earth on End” is not a copy
events of war and uprising, but a schematized military-revolutionary action.
There are military detachments on the stage, moving: a real car, motorcycles,
bicycles. Lighting is provided by military spotlights. In all eight episodes
Dah plays, illuminated propaganda posters give shocking fighting slogans. S. M. Tretyakov pro-
also carried out work on speech editing; the word is organized in the direction of greatest
talent and expressiveness. The agitational nature of the play is intensified and emphasized everywhere.
| this gives the play a number of moments of deep tragedy and, on the other hand, acute
satires. “The Land on End” is an exceptional success among workers, Red Army soldiers and students.
working proletarians. h

This is the production of the Meyerhold Theater. But the organizational side also has
zcesis of great importance. The fact is that all the actors of the Vs. Meyerhold—
students of the Workshop Vs. Meyerhold. This workshop is made up of three parts:
a group of comrades with professional acting experience and students of Gi I

courses. “Profacters”, to which the performers of the “Magnanimous Ro-
messenger“, constituted the Workshop of Vs. Meyerhold under GVYTM (State
Higher Theater Workshops), and students of the PI course are the main course of this university
(1921-1922).

In the fall of 1922, GVYTM was merged with the State Institute of Music
Noy Drama (GIMDRA)—GITIS (State Institute of Theatrical Theater) was formed
art). But very soon life showed that the joint work of these two
organizations is impossible - the fundamental differences are too great:
‘Movtsy came to GITIS with a certain revolutionary theatrical ideology,
and the Himdrovites were at the mercy of the most unfounded aesthetic prejudices -
cov. V. E. Meyerhold left GITIS, and behind him his entire Workshop, his entire course
(6. GVYTM), all the director’s and “most of the acting department of the 1st year (introductory
drinking at GITIS in the same autumn of 1922). These groups formed the current Ma-
Meyerhold's theater, which was entirely included in the work of the Meyerhold Theater. Peripeteia
The break with GITIS dragged on for six months and is still not over. This is
on the one hand, it was the reason that academic work, brilliantly started
in GVYTM*e, could not be carried out on a large scale in Meyerhold’s Workshop.
Another reason was the extremely difficult situation of the Theater and Workshop:
even the refusal of the entire artistic staff of the Theater from any payment for work
made it impossible to finish the season without a deficit. The theater was always standing in front of
threat of closure due to lack of funds (no subsidies from either the Theater or the Master
they do not receive) and a huge debt, and now this danger is not eliminated
dilated. ‚

All the enormous work of organizing again and maintaining existence

lives in extremely difficult material conditions.

Meyerhold's workshop is an exclusively ideologically welded organization
nation not only in its artistic views, but also in its political
beliefs
