an organization that combines production, academic and educational
practical and instructive work. The forms of theatrical action developed by her

with the works of Sun. Meyerhold, (if some of them distort the line of these ra-

vital tasks of the working class, such as making theater an instrument of communist propaganda
tion, and moving towards the merger of theater with life, i.e. to the transformation of theatrical me-
methods in methods of organizing social dynamics. The tasks of the Theater Vs. Meyerholtz—

a firm line ensures his future. b

Greece.

In Athens and Thessaloniki, under the organizations of the Communist Party there is
There are drama clubs. In Athens, their main composition is members of the youth and
women's organizations; they stage Greek and translated plays. Thessaloniki circle,
consisting of workers, staged plays such as “Resurrection” by L. Tolstoy,
“Bad Shepherds” by Mirbo and plays by Greek authors. The authorities are persecuting in every possible way
these circles, which arouse great interest among the working masses, who
definitely need their own theater. The Communist Party released a collection
nickname of revolutionary poems “Red Sands”; most of the authors are Greek
Chinese workers; It is interesting to note that almost half of the poems are dedicated to So-
Vetsky Russia.

Portugal.

Odone of the more prominent contemporary writers Manuel Ribeiro is an active
Communist Party worker. His novels “Cathedral” and “Desert” draw
the story of a socialist who fell under the influence of Catholicism. The last part of this
trilogy - “Renaissance”, not yet completed, gives the hero’s return to the revolution
tion work. After the first two books, which were criticized by party to-
comrades for the emerging religious trend, the last novel, undoubtedly,
straightens the revolutionary line. Leftist art began to penetrate into Portugal
Lyu: several books of leftist poets and magazines of new art have been published. There were
three exhibitions of futuristic painting; exists. organization of left-wing artists
cov. Artistic work among the working class is just beginning: the beginning
put, on the one hand, by anarchists, on the other, by radical intellectuals
group “New Harvest”. The first organized the “Free Theater” with the original
repertoire, the latter staged, among other things, Jaime Cortezao’s play “Adam and
Eva” with a rather unclear revolutionary tendency. Communist Party,
still very young, only now beginning to put cult work on the order of the day.

THE BEGINNINGS OF PROLETNULT IN ENGLAND.
(From a letter to the Chairman of the Central Committee of the All-Russian Proletkult).

Dear comrade, I was extremely pleased to receive your letter.
and I thank you from the bottom of my heart for the literature you sent me, from which I am trying
translate something immediately.

For my part, I will send you a copy of the book by Eden and Tsedar Paul
"Proletkult" and likewise any other literature that may be of interest
fresh for you and other Russian comrades. :

The proletcult movement here has not yet been molded into any complete
form. There is no corresponding organization yet, but for a number of years
There is a strong movement here, grouped around the so-called
“Plebs League” and pursuing the goal of educating the masses in the proletarian-class spirit,
mainly through familiarization with economic history and eco- theory
nomic science. So far, however, no serious efforts have been made to
artistic or cultural organizations. ...(?) among the workers. PS

“Nevertheless, there are a number of comrades here who, I am sure, with
They will be very enthusiastic about collaborating in the creation of the Rona, believe me,
new proletarian organization. We, in London, have already held a meeting of these
comrades. I hope that we will soon be able to bring our aspirations to fruition.
specific organizational forms.

I can see the following paths to lay the foundation of our
work. First of all, it is necessary to popularize the revolutionary proletarians

No. 8 CHRONICLE. 283

Russian songs translated from Russian, German, French and other languages. Then
we need to turn to creating good banners for the localsbranches of trade unions
and other workers' organizations, providing them with appropriate revolutionary
slogans. Further, it seems to me advisable to organize in workers
clubs of cultural (?) groups, which during the winter months could stage
in various clubs small dramatic things, as well as the creation of singing
societies, etc. Along with this, it is necessary to win more space in the party
printing for proletarian poetry and graphics.

What do you think about all this? Give me all your instructions. relative
specifically one or another form of identifying our movement.

If you can tell me more precisely what is in the area of interest to us
will be made in Russia over the coming months, I, in turn, will make
I do my best to coordinate my efforts with yours here. From
everything that I tell you above, it will be clear to you that we are still in the embryonic
nal condition.

With friendly greetings
Tom Quelch.

CZECHO - SLOVAKIAN PROLETKULT.

The Czecho-Slovak Proletkult arose at the end of 1920-21. and was founded
as part of the Communist Party in Czechoslovakia.

Previously, there were only Pr-ta cells in some large organizations
tions of the Party, which were later liquidated when the Party was created
Proletkult. Now we have 17 provincial and 67 seats in the whole of Czechoslovakia.
new Proletkults, and the movement is growing all the time. Proletkult is organized at
centralistic principles. Its Chairman is jointly the Secretary of the Party
for cultural affairs. The Cultural Council was founded to resolve cultural issues.
A council that has only an advisory vote, but has a casting vote
Executive Committee of the Party. The weekly Proletkult is published. Czecho-Slovakian problem
Prospect: firstly, the Czech-Slovak Prospect is an organization for the development of proletarian
culture (?). And, secondly, the political and educational organization of the Party.

Within the Party, Proletkult has great autonomy, only the most important
All issues are resolved by the Executive Committee of the Party. Ideologically, Czecho-
Slovaksky Prospekt accepts ttheses and resolutions of the Russian Prospect, but adapted
adapts them to the conditions of the country,

The ideological program of Proletkult has not yet been worked out, but
because Czecho-Slovaksky Prospekt is a very young organization that does not have
such experience as the Russian Proletkult. In the field of views on artistic
The shape of the Avenue is closely connected with the young revolutionary art of Czechoslovakia.

The activity of the Czech-Slovak Avenue is very large. A series of lectures was organized
both in Prague and in the provinces, on the topics: proletarian culture, socialism and
culture, history of socialist culture, Russian Proletkult, etc. d.

The Provincial Avenue, the Communist University, was established in Prague. commu-
nistic University of Czechoslovakia. The avenue has 4 departments. 1st department—History
socialism, 2nd department—Scientific socialism, 3rd department—Communist faction,
4th department - Communist culture. The University's lecturers are the best
comrades, both intellectuals and workers; e.g.: Shmeral, Gais, Naiman, Gora,
Whiteauer et al.

Next year the University program will be further expanded, mainly
in a significant way in the field of proletarian culture. Czecho-Slovaksky Prospekt has its own

142,
284 ye, ai" No. 3

a publishing house that does its job very well. First issue of Czecho-
Slovaksky Prospect - a collection of revolutionary poems by Czecho-Slovak and foreign
strange proletarian poets.

In general, we can say that Czecho-Slovak Avenue, which is rapidly developing
emerges, becomes a powerful instrument of communism in Czechoslovakia and, at the same time,
honestly fulfills his duty in the field of creating proletarian culture.

K. Internsky.

Editor: Editorial Eolleya.
